وإن كانت دار بين ثلاثة نفر فحفر أحدهم فيها بعيراً أو الحفر كان بغير رضا الشريكين الآخرين أو بنى حائطا فعطب به إنسان فعليه ثلثا الدية على عاقلته وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا عليه نصف الدية على عاقلته في الفصلين

ترجمہ اور اگر گھر تین آدمیوں کے درمیان ہو پس ان میں سے ایک نے اس میں کنواں کھودا اور کھودنا دونوں شریکوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر ہو یا دیوار بنائی پس اس میں کوئی آدمی بلاک ہو گیا تو اس کے اوپر دو ثلث دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اس پر آدھی دیت ہے اس کے عاقلہ پر دونوں صورتیں ہیں۔

تشریح تین شخصوں کا ایک گھر ہے ان میں سے ایک نے دو ساتھیوں کی رضا مندی کے بغیر اس میں کنواں کھودا ، یا دیوار بنائی اور اس کنویں میں کوئی آدمی مر گیا یا اس دیوار کی وجہ سے کوئی شخص مر گیا تو یہ دیوار بنانے والا یا کنواں کھودنے والا دو ثلث دیت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نصف دیت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ گویا کہ امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ شریک اپنے دونوں ساتھیوں کے حصہ میں تعدی کرنے کی وجہ سے ظالم ہے اور اپنے حصہ میں وہ ظالم نہیں ہے لہذا اپنے حصہ کا اس پر کوئی ممان نہ ہو گا۔ اور اپنے ساتھیوں کے حصہ میں تعدی کرنے کی وجہ سے ضامن ہوگا اور چونکہ ان کا حصہ ۲/۳ ہے اسلئے یہ دیت کے ۲/۳ کا ضامن ہوگا۔

صاحبین کی دلیل

لهما أن التلف بنصيب من أشهد عليه معتبر و بنصيب من لم يشهد عليه هدر فكانا قسمين فانقسم نصفين كما مر في عقر الأسد ونهس الحية وجرح الرجل

ترجمہ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس پر اشتہار ہوا ہے اس کے حصہ کے مقابلے میں تلف معتبر ہے اور جس پر اشہاد نہیں ہوا اس کے حصہ کے مقابلہ میں بدر ہے تو یہ دو قسمیں ہو گئیں تو ضمان آدھا آدھا منقسم ہو گا جیسے گذر گیا شیر کے زخمی کرنے میں اور سانپ کے ڈسنے میں اور آدمی کے زخمی کرنے ہیں ۔

تشریح یہ صاحبین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہاں ایک پر اشتہار ہوا ہے باقیوں پر نہیں ہوا تو اول پر منمان ہوگا اور باقیوں پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح جس نے کنواں کھودا، اس نے تعدی کی اور جنہوں نے نہیں کھودا ، انہوں نے کوئی تعدی نہیں کی۔ خلاصہ کلام یہاں ان دونوں مثالوں میں فعل دو ستم کے ہو گئے ایک وہ جس میں تعدی ہے اور دوسرا وہ جس میں تعدی نہیں ہے۔ لہذا انمان بھی دو ہی حصوں پر منقسم ہوگا تو نصف زمان کو ادا کرنا اس متعدی کا فریضہ ہوگا اور باقی بدر ہوگا۔

اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے کہ زید کو شیر نے پھاڑا اور سانپ نے اس کو ڈسا اور کسی شخص نے اس کو زخمی کیا اور ان تینوں کی وجہ سے وہ مر گیا تو جارح شخص پر آدھا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اس دلیل سے جو مذکور ہوئی۔

امام صاحب کی دلیل

وله أن الموت حصل بعلة واحدة وهو الثقل المقدر والعمق المقدر لأن أصل ذالك ليس بعلة وهو القليل حتى يعتبر كل جزء علة فيجتمع العلل وإذا كان كذالك يضاف إلى العلة الواحدة ثم تقسم على أربابها بقدر الملك بخلاف الجراحات فإن كل جراحة علة التلف بنفسها صغرت أو كبرت على ما عرف إلا أن عند المزاحمة أضيف إلى الكل لعدم الأولوية.

ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موت ایک علت سے حاصل ہوئی اور وہ نقل مقدر اور عمق مقدر ہے اس لئے کہ اصل نقل و عمق علت نہیں ہے اور وہ ( اصل ثقل) قلیل ہے یہاں تک کہ ہر جز علت ہوگا تو عمل جمع ہو جائیں گی۔ اور جب بات یوں ہے تو موت ایک علت کی طرف مضاف ہوگی پھر اس ایک علت کو اس کے اصحاب پر بقدر ملک تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا بخلاف جراحات کے اس لئے کہ ہر جراحت بذات خود تلف کی علت ہے چھوٹی ہو یا بڑی اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو پہچان لیا گیا ہے مگر مزاحمت کے وقت موت کل کی جانب مضاف ہوگی اولیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے نہ

تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں بقدر تعدی اس پر ضمان ہوگا اور پہلی صورت میں اس کی تعدی فقط ۱/۵ میں ہے لہذا اتنا ہی اس پر ضمان واجب ہوا ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اس کی تعدی دو ثلت میں ہے لہذا دو ثلث عمان واجب ہوا اور صاحبین نے جو مقیس علیہ پیش کیا ہے وہ اس مقام سے جوڑ نہیں کھاتا۔ بلکہ وہاں دو قسمیں کرنے پر مجبوری ہے اس لئے اس کی دو قسمیں کر کے اس پر نصف ضمان واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ اب اس کو عبارت سے ملاتے ہوئے چلئے ۔

امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرنے والا جو مرا تو اس کی موت کی علت ایک ہے علل متعددہ نہیں ہیں۔ یعنی دیوار کا مخصوص نقل اور کنویں کی مخصوصاً گہرائی ورنہ معمولی ثقل اور معمولی عمق سے عموماً موت واقع نہیں ہوتی لہذا عقل و عمق کے ہر ہر جز کو الگ الگ علت شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا ورنہ تو علل متعددہ جمع ہو جائیں گی بلکہ علت فقط مخصوص و مقدر ثقل و عمق ہے ورنہ اصل نقل و عشق یعنی معمولی قاتل نہیں ہوتا۔ تو وہ موت کی علت بھی نہ ہو گا لہذا اقلیل نقل و عمق علت نہ ہوگا ورنہ ہر جز کو الگ الگ علت ماننے سے بہت سی علتیں جمع ہو جائیں گی۔ بہر حال علت صرف ایک ہے اور وہ مخصوص و مقدر نقل اور عمق ہے۔ تو یہی موت کی علت ہے اس کی جانب موت کی اضافت ہوگی۔ پھر ار باب دار پر بند ر ملک یہ ایک علت تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ لہذا صورت اولی میں قسمت مذکورہ کے نتیجہ میں اس ایک پر دیت کا۱/۵ واجب ہوا ۔ کیونکہ اس کی ملکیت اتنی ہی ہے۔ لہذا اگر ان پانچوں پر اشہاد کیا جاتا اور وہ دیوار ٹھیک نہ کرے تب بھی ان میں سے ہر ایک پر دیت کا ۱/۵ ہی واجب ہوتا کہ لہذا اب بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں جب علت واحدہ کو ان تینوں پر تقسیم کہ تو کنواں کھودنے والے اور دیوار بنانے والے کی تعدی فقط دونگٹ میں ہے اور اپنے ثلث میں اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہیں
Book of Diyat. Three partners had a house; one of them dug a well or built a wall without the consent of the other two, and someone died from it. How much diyat is obligatory on that person? Statements of the jurists. "And if a house is between three persons, and one of them digs a well in it, or the digging was without the consent of the other two partners, or he built a wall and a person perished thereby, then upon him is two-thirds of the diyah on his 'aqilah. This is according to Abu Hanifah. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: upon him is half of the diyah on his 'aqilah in both cases." Translation: And if a house is among three persons, then one of them dug a well in it, and the digging was without the consent of the other two partners, or built a wall, then a person was killed in it, then upon him is two-thirds of the diyah on his 'aqilah. That is according to Imam Abu Hanifah. And the Sahibayn said that upon him is half the diyah on his 'aqilah in both cases. Commentary: Three persons have a house; one of them dug a well or built a wall without the consent of the two companions, and a person died in that well or due to that wall. Then this wall-builder or well-digger will be liable for two-thirds of the diyah. This is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifah. According to the Sahibayn, he will be liable for half the diyah. It is as if Imam Sahib says: This partner, due to his transgression in the shares of his two companions, is a wrongdoer, and in his own share he is not a wrongdoer. Therefore, there is no liability on him for his own share. And due to transgression in his companions' shares, he will be liable, and since their share is 2/3, he will be liable for 2/3 of the diyah. Proof of the Sahibayn: "For them (the Sahibayn) is that the loss is considered valid in respect of the share of the one against whom evidence was brought, and is disregarded in respect of the share of whom evidence was not brought; thus they become two parts, so it is divided into halves, as passed in the case of a lion's scratching, a snake's biting, and a man's wounding." Translation: The proof of the Sahibayn is that the loss is considered valid against the share of the one for whom notification was made, and is disregarded against the share of whom no notification was made. So they became two divisions, so the liability is divided into halves, as passed in the case of a lion's scratching, a snake's biting, and a man's wounding. Commentary: This is the proof of the Sahibayn, the summary of which is that here notification was made for one, not for the others; so liability is on the first, and no liability on the others. Similarly, the one who dug the well transgressed, and those who did not dig did not commit any transgression. In short, in both examples, the act became of two types: one with transgression and the other without transgression. Therefore, liability will also be divided into two parts, so half the liability is the duty of the transgressor, and the rest is disregarded. Its example is exactly that Zaid was mauled by a lion, bitten by a snake, and wounded by a man, and due to these three he died; then half the liability is obligatory on the person who wounded. This is the proof that was mentioned. Proof of Imam Sahib: "And for him (Abu Hanifah) is that death occurred from one cause, which is the specific weight and specific depth, because the origin of that is not a cause, and it is slight; so that every part becomes a cause, thus the causes join. And if it is so, then it is attributed to the one cause, then it is divided among its owners according to ownership, contrary to wounds, because every wound is by itself a cause of the loss, whether small or large, according to what is known; except that at the time of competition it is attributed to the whole due to lack of priority." Translation: And Abu Hanifah's proof is that death occurred from one cause, and that is the specified weight and specified depth, because the original weight and depth are not a cause, and that (original weight) is slight; until every part becomes a cause, so the causes collect. And when it is so, then death is attributed to the one cause, then that one cause is divided among its owners according to ownership, unlike wounds, because every wound is by itself a cause of loss, whether small or large, according to the detail that has been recognized; except that at the time of competition, death is attributed to the whole due to lack of priority. Commentary: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifah, the summary of which is that in both cases, liability is upon him according to the extent of transgression. In the first case, his transgression is only in 1/5, so only that much liability is obligatory. And in the second case, his transgression is in two-thirds, so two-thirds liability is obligatory. And the analogy that the Sahibayn presented does not fit this place; rather, there is compulsion to make two divisions, so they divided it into two and made half liability obligatory. Now, drawing this in line with the text: The proof of Imam Sahib is that the death of the deceased occurred from one cause, not multiple causes. That is, the specific weight of the wall and the specific depth of the well; otherwise, ordinary weight and ordinary depth do not generally cause death. Therefore, every part of weight and depth will not be counted as a separate cause; otherwise multiple causes would collect. Rather, the cause is only the specific and predetermined weight and depth; otherwise, the original weight and depth (ordinary) are not killers. So that would not be a cause of death; hence the lesser weight and depth are not causes; otherwise, if every part were considered a separate cause, many causes would collect. In any case, the cause is only one, and that is the specific and predetermined weight and depth. So this is the cause of death; death will be attributed to it. Then, for the owners of the house according to ownership, this one cause will be divided. Therefore, in the first case, as a result of the mentioned division, one-fifth of the diyah became obligatory on the one (who built), because his ownership is that much. So if all five had been notified and they did not fix the wall, then also upon each of them one-fifth of the diyah would be obligatory. Therefore, now also it will be like that. And in the second case, when the single cause is divided among the three, then the transgression of the well-digger and wall-builder is only in two-thirds, and in his own third there is no transgression from his side.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the liability of a partner who causes death by digging a well or building a wall on shared property without the consent of the other partners. The core issue is how to apportion the diyat (blood money) when the harmful act is performed by one partner. According to Abu Hanifah, the liable partner must pay two-thirds of the diyat if there are three partners, because his transgression extends only to the shares of the other two; his own share is not subject to liability. The Sahibayn, on the other hand, hold that he must pay only half, reasoning that the loss should be divided into two halves: one half for the share with transgression (his own share and the shares of those who consented? Actually, they treat the act as having two aspects: the part with transgression and the part without. They analogize to a case where a lion, snake, and a man all contribute to death: only half the diyat is imposed on the man because the lion and snake are not liable. The text explains both proofs in detail. Imam Abu Hanifah's proof focuses on the unity of the cause: death is caused by the specific weight or depth, which is a single cause, not multiple. Therefore, the liability is divided according to ownership shares. The Sahibayn's proof considers that the act is divisible into two categories: the part where the doer transgressed (by acting without consent) and the part where he did not (his own ownership). The commentary clarifies the reasoning and emphasizes that the analogy of multiple independent tortfeasors does not apply here because the cause is one. The passage ultimately does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi (relied upon), but it presents both positions with their evidence.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money payable to the heirs of a victim of wrongful death or injury.
عاقلة (aabil): The group of male agnates (asabah) who are responsible for paying diyah on behalf of the killer in accidental cases.
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression; acting beyond one's rights, e.g., using shared property without consent, causing harm.
اشهاد / أشهد (ishhad / ashada): To notify or give witness; in this context, it refers to the notification of the partner's act to the others, or the concept of bearing witness to the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, if three partners own a house and one digs a well without the others' consent, causing death, what fraction of the diyah is the digger liable for?
A) Half
B) Two-thirds
C) One-third
D) The entire diyah

Key Takeaway
The apportionment of diyat in joint property torts differs between Abu Hanifah (by ownership shares) and the Sahibayn (by nature of transgression), reflecting a deeper usul difference on the unity of the cause.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Imam Abu Hanifa's Proof on Proportionate Liability for Composite Causes of Death
Imam Abu Hanifa presents his proof on proportionate liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's proof for proportionate liability in composite cause death and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's analogy to independent wounds.

Core Idea
When death results from a single composite cause, liability is proportional to each party's contribution — not equal.

In the Hanafi school, liability (daman) for death can be apportioned differently depending on whether the cause is single and composite or multiple and independent. This lesson unpacks Imam Abu Hanifa's proof for the case of a wall and a well that together cause a death, showing why he rejects the Sahibayn's analogy to multiple wounds. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply causal reasoning in tort liability.

Guided Path
1
State the legal issue
Identify the scenario: multiple parties contribute to a single death through a composite cause (e.g., a wall and a well). The question is how to apportion blood money (diyah).
The composite cause is the measured weight (thiql) and depth (umq) together; individually they are not lethal.
2
Present Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that death is caused by one composite cause. Liability is divided proportionally according to each party's share in that cause (ownership or transgression).
For example, if a person owns 1/5 of the cause, he pays 1/5 of the diyah.
3
Present the Sahibayn's opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad analogize to multiple independent wounds, where each wound is an independent cause of death. In that case, liability is equal among all actionable causes when no priority exists.
This analogy would lead to equal division (e.g., half each) rather than proportional.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy because in the composite case, the components are not independently lethal – they only cause death when combined. In the wound case, each wound can kill alone. Therefore the ruling differs.
This is a critical distinction in the illa (effective cause).
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a person may owe 1/5 or 2/3 of diyah; under the Sahibayn, they would owe half each in a two-party scenario.
The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's view.

وله أن الموت حصل بعلة واحدة وهو الثقل المقدر والعمق المقدر لأن أصل ذالك ليس بعلة وهو القليل حتى يعتبر كل جزء علة فيجتمع العلل وإذا كان كذالك يضاف إلى العلة الواحدة ثم تقسم على أربابها بقدر الملك بخلاف الجراحات فإن كل جراحة علة التلف بنفسها صغرت أو كبرت على ما عرف إلا أن عند المزاحمة أضيف إلى الكل لعدم الأولوية.
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موت ایک علت سے حاصل ہوئی اور وہ فقل مقدر اور عمق مقدر ہے اس لئے کہ اصل نقل و عمق علت نہیں ہے اور وہ ( اصل ثقل) قلیل ہے یہاں تک کہ ہر جز علت ہوگا تو عمل جمع ہو جائیں گی۔ اور جب بات یوں ہے تو موت ایک علت کی طرف مضاف ہوگی پھر اس ایک علت کو اس کے اصحاب پر بقدر ملک تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا بخلاف جراحات کے اس لئے کہ ہر جراحت بذات خود تلف کی علت ہے چھوٹی ہو یا بڑی اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو پہچان لیا گیا ہے مگر مزاحمت کے وقت موت کل کی جانب مضاف ہوگی اولیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے نہ
تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں بقدر تعدی اس پر ضمان ہوگا اور پہلی صورت میں اس کی تعدی فقط ۱/۵ میں ہے لہذا اتنا ہی اس پر ضمان واجب ہوا ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اس کی تعدی دو ثلت میں ہے لہذا دو ثلث عمان واجب ہوا اور صاحبین نے جو مقیس علیہ پیش کیا ہے وہ اس مقام سے جوڑ نہیں کھاتا۔ بلکہ وہاں دو قسمیں کرنے پر مجبوری ہے اس لئے اس کی دو قسمیں کر کے اس پر نصف ضمان واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ اب اس کو عبارت سے ملاتے ہوئے چلئے ۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرنے والا جو مرا تو اس کی موت کی علت ایک ہے علل متعددہ نہیں ہیں۔ یعنی دیوار کا مخصوص نقل اور کنویں کی مخصوصاً گہرائی ورنہ معمولی ثقل اور معمولی عمق سے عموماً موت واقع نہیں ہوتی لہذا عقل و عمق کے ہر ہر جز کو الگ الگ علت شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا ورنہ تو علل متعددہ جمع ہو جائیں گی بلکہ علت فقط مخصوص و مقدر ثقل و عمق ہے ورنہ اصل نقل و عشق یعنی معمولی قاتل نہیں ہوتا۔ تو وہ موت کی علت بھی نہ ہو گا لہذا اقلیل نقل و عمق علت نہ ہوگا ورنہ ہر جز کو الگ الگ علت ماننے سے بہت سی علتیں جمع ہو جائیں گی۔ بہر حال علت صرف ایک ہے اور وہ مخصوص و مقدر نقل اور عمق ہے۔ تو یہی موت کی علت ہے اس کی جانب موت کی اضافت ہوگی۔ پھر ار باب دار پر بند ر ملک یہ ایک علت تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ لہذا صورت اولی میں قسمت مذکورہ کے نتیجہ میں اس ایک پر دیت کا۱/۵ واجب ہوا ۔ کیونکہ اس کی ملکیت اتنی ہی ہے۔ لہذا اگر ان پانچوں پر اشہاد کیا جاتا اور وہ دیوار ٹھیک نہ کرے تب بھی ان میں سے ہر ایک پر دیت کا ۱/۵ ہی واجب ہوتا کہ لہذا اب بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں جب علت واحدہ کو ان تینوں پر تقسیم کہ تو کنواں کھودنے والے اور دیوار بنانے والے کی تعدی فقط دونگٹ میں ہے اور اپنے ثلث میں اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اس کا ضمان بھی اس پر واجب نہ ہوگا، بخلاف جراحات مذکورہ کے کہ شیر نے بھی اس کو پھاڑا ہو اور سانپ نے اس کوڈ سا بھی ہو اور کسی شخص نے اس کو زخمی بھی کیا ہو۔
کیونکہ یہاں ہر فعل اپنی جگہ ایک مستقل علت ہے کیونکہ یہ تین چیزیں ایسی ہیں جن سے آدمی تلف ہو جاتا ہے لہذا یہ مستقل علتیں ہیں چھوٹی ہو یا بڑی۔
اب جب ان تینوں کا اجتماع ہو گیا اور ان تینوں کے درمیان مزاحمت ہوئی تو چونکہ اولیت تو ہے نہیں کہ وہ مقدم ہے اور وہ مؤخر ہے یا وہ مؤخر ہے یا وہ اصلی علت ہے اور وہ اصلی نہیں ہے تو موت کی اضافت ان میں سے ہر ایک کی جانب کی گئی یعنی ان میں سے ہر ایک کی وجہ سے وہ مرا ہے اس کے بعد ہم نے اس پر غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ شیر اور سانپ کا فعل تو ایسا ہے جس کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور آدمی کا فعل ایسا ہے جس کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا ہم نے یہاں بدرجہ، مجبوری فعل کی دوقسمیں کر دیں ایک مضمون اور دوسرا غیر مضمون تو ہم نے مضمون کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے نصف ضمان زخمی کرنے والے شخص پر واجب کر دیا ہے۔
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: He said: Death occurs by one cause, which is the measured weight and measured depth, because the origin of that is not a cause, which is the small amount, so that each part would be considered a cause and the causes would combine. If that is so, it is attributed to the one cause, then divided among its owners according to ownership, unlike wounds, for each wound is a cause of destruction by itself, small or large, as known. However, when there is competition, it is attributed to all due to lack of priority. Translation: The proof of Abu Hanifa is that death results from one cause, which is the measured weight and depth, because the original weight and depth are not causes, and the original weight is small, so that each part would be a cause, then the causes would combine. When it is so, death is attributed to one cause, then that one cause is divided among its owners according to ownership. Unlike wounds, because each wound is itself a cause of destruction, small or large, according to the detail known. But at the time of competition, death is attributed to all due to lack of priority. Commentary: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa, the summary of which is that in both cases, liability is to the extent of transgression. In the first case, his transgression is only in 1/5, so that much liability is imposed. In the second case, his transgression is in 2/3, so 2/3 of the blood money is imposed. The Sahibayn's analogy that they presented does not connect here. Rather, they were forced to make two divisions, so they divided it into two and imposed half liability on him. Now continue in alignment with the text. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the death that occurred has one cause, not multiple causes. That is, the specific weight of the wall and the specific depth of the well; otherwise, ordinary weight and ordinary depth do not generally cause death. Therefore, each individual part of weight and depth is not considered a separate cause, otherwise many causes would combine. Rather, the cause is only the specific and measured weight and depth. Thus, death is attributed to this one cause. Then that one cause is divided among its owners according to ownership. So in the first scenario, as a result of the mentioned division, one person owes 1/5 of the blood money, because his ownership is that much. If all five were witnesses and he did not fix the wall, each would owe 1/5. In the second scenario, when the single cause is divided among the three, the transgression of the well-digger and wall-builder is only in two-thirds, and in his own third there is no transgression, so he is not liable. This is unlike the mentioned wounds, where a lion tore, a snake bit, and a person wounded. Because here each act is an independent cause, since these three things individually cause destruction. When they all combined and competed, and since there is no priority, death is attributed to each. But upon consideration, the lion and snake's actions do not incur liability, while the human's action does. So out of necessity, the acts were divided into two: actionable and non-actionable. Taking the actionable, half liability is imposed on the wounding person.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Hanifa presents his proof (dalil) for proportionate liability when multiple parties contribute to a single death through a composite cause. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) had analogized to the case of multiple independent wounds, where each wound is an independent cause, leading to equal liability. Imam Abu Hanifa rejects this analogy. He argues that in the case of a wall and a well, the death is caused by a single composite cause: the specific weight and depth combined. Each part alone would not cause death, so the cause is unitary. Therefore, liability is divided proportionally according to each person's share of the cause (by ownership or contribution). In the first scenario (five responsible for the wall), the person's transgression is only in one-fifth, so he owes one-fifth of the blood money. In the second scenario (three people: wall builder, well digger, and a third), the first two are responsible for two-thirds, and the third is not liable since his share had no transgression. Imam Abu Hanifa contrasts this with the example of a lion, snake, and human attacker, where each act is an independent cause of death. Since the lion and snake's acts are not compensable in Islamic law (they are not liable), and the human's is, the liability is divided by necessity: here the human bears half the blood money because his act is one of two actionable causes (the other being non-actionable). The author of the commentary (the sharh) explains that the Sahibayn's qiyas (analogy) to independent wounds does not fit this case; rather, they were forced into a two-division approach.

Key Terms
علة (illa): The effective cause (sabab) of death; here, the specific weight and depth that together cause death.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or exceeding proper bounds; the basis for liability in torts.
ضمان (daman): Liability or surety; here specifically the obligation to pay blood money (diyah).
مزاحمة (muzahamah): Competition or conflict among multiple causes; when causes compete and there is no priority, death is attributed to all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, why does he reject the Sahibayn's analogy to multiple independent wounds?
A) Because wounds cannot be compared to walls and wells.
B) Because each wound is an independent cause, while in the wall and well case the components are not independently lethal.
C) Because the Sahibayn's view leads to injustice.
D) Because the proof is based on a hadith.

Key Takeaway
When death results from a single composite cause, liability is divided proportionally according to each party's share in that cause, not equally as with independent causes.

Rider's Liability for Animal Actions: The Rule of Controllability
Chapter heading and initial ruling on rider's liability for animal actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven cases where a rider is liable for animal-caused harm and the two exceptions, and apply the controllability principle to scenario-based questions.

Core Idea
A rider is liable for controllable animal actions, but not for sudden kicks or tail strikes.

This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir establishes the Hanafi ruling on a rider's liability for harm caused by a ridden animal. The key distinction is controllability: the rider can guide the animal's forward movement and avoid obstacles, but cannot predict sudden backward kicks or tail movements. Knowing these exceptions ensures correct application of diyat rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
The rider (raakib) is liable (damin) for harm caused by the animal's actions that he can control. The text lists these actions: treading, striking with foreleg, striking with hind leg, striking with head, biting, butting, and pushing.
These seven actions are considered controllable because the rider is responsible for directing the animal.
2
Learn the Exceptions
The rider is NOT liable for two specific actions: a sudden kick with the hind leg (najh) and striking with the tail. These are deemed uncontrollable reflexes.
Memorize: liable for 7, not liable for 2.
3
Apply to a Scenario
For any given scenario, first determine which action caused the harm. If it is one of the seven liable actions, the rider must compensate. If it is a kick or tail strike, the rider is not liable.
Use the list as a checklist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ جنايه البَهِيمَةِ وَالجَنايَةِ عَلَيْهَا
ترجمہ یہ باب ہے چوپائے کی جنایت اور چوپائے پر جنایت کے بیان میں
تشریح اس باب میں یہ بیان ہو گا کہ اگر چوپائے نے کسی کے ساتھ کچھ حرکت کر دی، اور نقصان پہنچا دیا تو منمان کی کیا صورت ہوگی ؟ اور اگر چوپائے پر کسی نے جنایت کی تو اس کا کیا حکم ہوگا ؟ جانور کسی کو روند دے اگلی یا پچھلی ٹانگوں سے یاڈم سے چوٹ لگا دے یا دھکا دے تو سوار اس کے نقصان کا ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں
قال الراكب ضامن لما أوطأت الدابة ما أصابت بيدها أو رجلها أو رأسها أو كدمت أو خبطت وكذا إذا صدمت ولا يضمن ما نفحت برجلها أو ذنبها
ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ سوار ضامن ہو گا اس کا جس کو چوپائے نے روندا ہوا گلے پاؤں سے روند ایا پچھلے پاؤں سے پیار اپنے سر سے یا کاٹا ہو یا اگلے پاؤں مارے ہوں اور ایسے ہی جب کہ دھکا دیا ہو اور ضامن نہ ہوگا کہ چوپائے نے اپنے پاؤں کے گھر مارے ہوں یا اپنی دم ۔
تشریح زید مثلاً اپنے گھوڑے پر بیٹھا ہوا جا رہا تھا اس کے گھوڑے نے خالد کو نقصان پہنچا کر ہلاک کر دیا تو مذکورہ صورتوں میں سے ایک کے اندر ضمان نہیں ہے اور باقیوں کے اندر ضمان ہے اگر گھوڑے نے لات یا دم ماری ہو تو ضمان نہ ہوگا اور باقی صورتوں میں ضمان واجب ہوگا وہ باقی صورتیں چھ ہیں۔
ا اپنے پاؤں سے روند نا
Chapter of Injury by the Animal and Injury upon It. Translation: This chapter is about the injury by an animal and injury upon an animal. Commentary: In this chapter, it will be stated that if an animal does something to someone and causes harm, what is the ruling? And if someone commits an injury upon an animal, what is the ruling? The animal tramples someone, strikes with forelegs or hind legs, or tail causes injury, or pushes, is the rider liable for the harm? He said: The rider is liable for what the animal tramples, what it strikes with its foreleg, hind leg, head, bites, butts, and likewise if it pushes. And he is not liable for what it kicks with its hind leg or its tail. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: The rider is liable for that which the animal tramples, whether with forelegs or hind legs, or with its head, or bites, or strikes with forelegs, and likewise when it pushes. And he is not liable for the animal striking with its hind leg or its tail. Commentary: For example, Zaid was riding his horse, and his horse caused harm to Khalid and killed him. In the mentioned situations, in one there is no liability, and in the rest there is liability. If the horse kicked or struck with its tail, there is no liability; in other cases, liability is obligatory. Those other cases are six: 1. Trampling with its feet.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This is the beginning of a new chapter in Kitab al-Diyat on injuries caused by animals and injuries upon animals. The passage presents the ruling of Muhammad al-Shaybani from al-Jami' al-Saghir: a rider is liable for harm caused by the animal's actions that the rider can control, such as trampling (with fore or hind feet), striking with the head, biting, butting, or pushing. The rider is not liable for actions that are typically not controllable, such as a sudden kick from the hind legs (najh) or a swish of the tail. The commentary elaborates with an example: if a rider's horse kills someone, the rider is liable if the harm resulted from any of the six controllable actions (the list begins with trampling), but not if from a kick or tail strike. The rationale is that the rider has control over the animal's forward movement and direction but not over unexpected backward kicks or tail motions.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): Liable; one who must compensate for harm caused.
راڪب (raakib): Rider; the person riding the animal.
نفحت (najah): Kicking with hind leg; an action that does not incur liability on the rider.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the chapter on animal injuries, when is the rider NOT liable for the animal's actions?
A) When the animal tramples someone.
B) When the animal bites someone.
C) When the animal kicks with its hind leg or strikes with its tail.
D) When the animal pushes someone.

Key Takeaway
A rider is liable for seven controllable actions of the animal but not for hind leg kicks or tail strikes, based on the principle of controllability in Hanafi fiqh.

Diyat — Blood Money

Liability Apportionment Among Multiple Concurrent Causes of Death
Concluding the ruling on shared liability among multiple direct causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when multiple independent causes of death include both liable and non-liable actors and explain why only the liable actor bears responsibility.

Core Idea
When causes converge, only liable causes matter; non-liable causes (animals) do not share the burden.

This passage from the Book of Diyat addresses a scenario where a lion, a snake, and a person all inflict injuries leading to death. The legal question: who bears the diyat? The Hanafi position is that each act is an independent cause, but since animals incur no liability, the human's act takes full responsibility—proportionally half the diyat. This illustrates key principles of causation and liability in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
The passage describes three actors: a lion, a snake, and a person. Each inflicts an injury, and the victim dies. The task is to determine liability for diyat.
2
Classify each act as an independent cause
The author states that each act is a 'mustaqill illah' (independent cause) because each can cause death. No priority or original cause exists among them.
3
Determine liability status of each cause
The acts of the lion and snake do not incur daman (liability) in Islamic law—animals are not legally responsible. The human act does incur liability.
4
Apply the principle of apportionment
Since the causes are simultaneous and independent, but only one is liable, the liability is assigned entirely to the liable cause. Out of necessity, the human act is considered liable and half the diyat is imposed.
Half is designated because the other two causes are non-liable; the human's act is treated as if it were half of the total causative factors.
5
State the concluded ruling
The mufta bihi: the person who wounded is liable for half the diyat. This resolves the conflict of causes by distinguishing between liable and non-liable actors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات
۲۲۸
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ ہے۔ لہذا اس کا ضمان بھی اس پر واجب نہ ہوگا، بخلاف جراحات مذکورہ کے کہ شیر نے بھی اس کو پھاڑا ہو اور سانپ نے اس کوڈ سا بھی ہو اور کسی شخص نے اس کو زخمی بھی کیا ہو۔
کیونکہ یہاں ہر فعل اپنی جگہ ایک مستقل علت ہے کیونکہ یہ تین چیزیں ایسی ہیں جن سے آدمی تلف ہو جاتا ہے لہذا یہ مستقل علتیں ہیں چھوٹی ہو یا بڑی۔
اب جب ان تینوں کا اجتماع ہو گیا اور ان تینوں کے درمیان مزاحمت ہوئی تو چونکہ اولیت تو ہے نہیں کہ وہ مقدم ہے اور وہ مؤخر ہے یا وہ مؤخر ہے یا وہ اصلی علت ہے اور وہ اصلی نہیں ہے تو موت کی اضافت ان میں سے ہر ایک کی جانب کی گئی یعنی ان میں سے ہر ایک کی وجہ سے وہ مرا ہے اس کے بعد ہم نے اس پر غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ شیر اور سانپ کا فعل تو ایسا ہے جس کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور آدمی کا فعل ایسا ہے جس کی وجہ سے ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا ہم نے یہاں بدرجہ، مجبوری فعل کی دوقسمیں کر دیں ایک مضمون اور دوسرا غیر
مضمون تو ہم نے مضمون کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے نصف ضمان زخمی کرنے والے شخص پر واجب کر دیا ہے۔
Book of Diyat. 228. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Sharh Hidaya Volume 15. Therefore, liability will not be obligatory upon him, contrary to the mentioned injuries, that the lion tore him, the snake bit him, and a person wounded him. Because here each act in its place is an independent cause, because these three things are such from which a person perishes, so they are independent causes, small or big. Now when these three combined and there was conflict between them, since there is no priority that one is earlier and one later, or one is the original cause and the other is not, then death is attributed to each of them, i.e., he died due to each of them. After that we considered and it became known that the act of the lion and snake is such that liability is not obligatory, and the act of the person is such that liability is obligatory. So here out of necessity we divided the act into two types: one with liability and one without liability. Then we considered the one with liability and made half of the liability obligatory upon the person who wounded.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a ruling on multiple concurrent causes of death. The author discusses a case where a lion, a snake, and a person all inflicted injuries on a victim, leading to death. The Hanafi ruling here is that each act is an independent cause (illat) since each is capable of causing death. However, since the acts of the lion and snake do not incur legal liability (daman) because animals are not legally responsible, only the human act is compensable. Therefore, the liability (half of the diyat) is imposed on the person who wounded, not on the animals. This is an application of the principle that when multiple causes converge and some are non-liable, the liable cause takes the full responsibility proportionally.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation, specifically blood money (diyat) in this context.
علت (illat): A cause that directly leads to death; an independent factor in the chain of causation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a lion, a snake, and a person all injuring a victim, why is half the diyat assigned to the person?
A) Because the person is the only one with legal capacity.
B) Because the acts of the lion and snake are not subject to liability, so the human's act takes full responsibility proportionally.
C) Because the lion and snake are considered indirect causes.
D) Because the person's wound was the primary cause.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on multiple concurrent causes of death: only liable actors bear responsibility, and the apportionment disregards non-liable causes.

Liability of a Rider for Injuries Caused by His Animal
Introducing the chapter on animal injuries and stating the ruling on rider's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rider liability and distinguish between avoidable and unavoidable animal acts.

Core Idea
A rider is liable for avoidable harm from the animal's front but not for unavoidable hind kicks.

This lesson opens the chapter on animal injuries. It presents a clear ruling from Imam Muhammad: the rider is liable for what the animal does with its front limbs, head, bite, or push, but not for hind leg kicks or tail strikes. The underlying principle is that public road use is permissible conditioned on safety, but only for foreseeable harm that the rider can avoid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and party
Determine that the ruling concerns a rider (raakib) and his liability (daman) for acts of the animal.
The rider is the person controlling the animal at the time of the incident.
2
Distinguish the two categories of acts
Classify animal acts into those caused by front limbs, head, bite, or push (liable) and those caused by hind leg kick or tail (not liable).
The key distinction is controllability.
3
Understand the principle: condition of safety
Passing on public roads is restricted to safe passage. This condition applies only to harm that can be avoided.
Avoidable harm: trampling, biting, pushing. Unavoidable: hind kick, tail strike.
4
Apply the principle to a scenario
Given a scenario, decide liability based on whether the act was controllable or not.
If the act is unavoidable, the condition of safety does not apply, so no liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ جنايه البَهِيمَةِ وَالجَنايَةِ عَلَيْهَا

قال الراكب ضامن لما أوطأت الدابة ما أصابت بيدها أو رجلها أو رأسها أو كدمت أو خبطت وكذا إذا صدمت ولا يضمن ما نفحت برجلها أو ذنبها

والأصل أن المرور فى طريق المسلمين مباح مقيد بشرط السلامة لأنه يتصرف في حقه من وجه وفي حق غيره من وجه لكونه مشتركا بين كل الناس فقلنا بالإباحة مقيدا بما ذكرنا ليعتدل النظر من الجانبين

ثم إنما يتقيد بشرط السلامة فيما يمكن الاحتراز عنه ولا يتقيد بها فيما لا يمكن التحرز عنه لما فيه من المنع عن التصرف وسد بابه وهو مفتوح والاحتراز عن الإيطاء وما يضاهيه ممكن فإنه ليس من ضرورات التيسير فقيدناه بشرط السلامة عنه والنفحة بالرجل والذنب ليس يمكنه الاحتراز عنه مع السير على الدابة فلم يتقيد به.
Chapter on Injury by Animals and Injury Upon Animals. He (Muhammad) said: The rider is liable for what the animal tramples, what it hits with its front leg or hind leg or head, or what it bites or kicks with front legs, and likewise if it pushes. And he is not liable for what it kicks with its hind leg or tail. And the principle is that passing through the roads of Muslims is permissible, restricted by the condition of safety, because he acts in his own right from one aspect and in the right of others from another aspect, due to it being shared among all people. So we said permissibility restricted by what we mentioned (i.e., safety) so that consideration is balanced from both sides. Then it is restricted by the condition of safety in what can be avoided, and it is not restricted by it in what cannot be avoided, because that would prevent action and close its door while it is open. Avoiding trampling and similar is possible, for it is not among the necessities of ease, so we restricted it by the condition of safety regarding it. But the kick with the hind leg or tail cannot be avoided while riding the animal, so it is not restricted by it.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on injuries caused by animals (bab jinaayat al-bahimah) and injuries upon animals. It begins with a matn from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, stating the ruling on a rider's liability. The rider is liable for injuries caused by the animal's front limbs (including trampling, hitting with front or hind legs, head, biting, and pushing) but not for kicks from hind legs or tail. The rationale is that the rider can control the front of the animal and is expected to avoid causing harm, whereas hind leg kicks and tail strikes are unpredictable and unavoidable. This is tied to a general principle about using public roads: passing is permissible but conditioned on safety. That condition applies only to avoidable harms; unavoidable harms (like hind kicks) are not conditioned on safety because they would effectively prohibit riding altogether.

Key Terms
راكب (raakib): Rider, the person riding the animal (horse, camel, etc.).
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation, specifically for property damage or bodily injury.
نفحت (nafahat): Kicked with hind leg or struck with tail.
مرور (murur): Passing, movement through a public road.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, for which of the following acts is the rider NOT liable?
A) The animal tramples a person with its front legs.
B) The animal bites someone.
C) The animal kicks with its hind leg.
D) The animal pushes a person.

Key Takeaway
The rider is liable only for animal acts that he can reasonably avoid; unpredictable acts like hind kicks carry no liability.

Liability for Animal-Caused Injuries on the Road
Explaining the general principle of liability for animal-caused injuries on the road

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of liability for animal-caused injuries on a public road and apply the avoidability criterion to determine when the rider is liable.

Core Idea
Liability depends on avoidability: avoidable harm → liable; unavoidable harm → not liable.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the delicate balance between the permissibility of using public roads and the duty to avoid harming others. The Hanafi school distinguishes between harms the rider can prevent and those inherent to riding. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying tort liability in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Recognize that passing on a Muslim road is permissible but conditioned on safety. This condition applies only to harms that can be avoided.
2
Understand the condition of safety
The condition of safety (shart al-salama) is not absolute; it applies only where avoidance (ihtiraz) is possible. If avoidance is impossible, the condition does not apply.
3
Apply the avoidability test to specific scenarios
For each type of harm (trampling, kicking, stopping, debris), determine whether the rider could have avoided it. If yes, liable; if no, not liable.
The text gives examples: trampling (avoidable→liable), hind leg kick (unavoidable→no liability), stopping (avoidable→liable), small debris (unavoidable→no liability), large stone (avoidable→liable).
4
Distinguish the rider and pillion-rider
The same ruling applies to both, because the legal reasoning (the ability to avoid) is identical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ الکلام ... دانت کے اگلے حصہ سے کاٹنا، بجہ اگلے پاؤں سے مارنا صدم دھکا دینا یعنی بدن سے گرانا، نلح کھڑ سے مارنا اور مطلق پاؤں سے مارنا ، لات مارنا اور چیز ہے اور روند نا اور چیز ہے۔
والأصل أن المرور فى طريق المسلمين مباح مقيد بشرط السلامة لأنه يتصرف في حقه من وجه وفي حق غيره من وجه لكونه مشتركا بين كل الناس فقلنا بالإباحة مقيدا بما ذكرنا ليعتدل النظر من الجانبين.
ثم إنما يتقيد بشرط السلامة فيما يمكن الاحتراز عنه ولا يتقيد بها فيما لا يمكن التحرز عنه لما فيه من المنع عن التصرف وسد بابه وهو مفتوح والاحتراز عن الإيطاء وما يضاهيه ممكن فإنه ليس من ضرورات التيسير فقيدناه بشرط السلامة عنه والنفحة بالرجل والذنب ليس يمكنه الاحتراز عنه مع السير على الدابة فلم يتقيد به.
فإن أوقفها في الطريق ضمن النفحة أيضا لأنه يمكنه التحرز عن الإيقاف وإن لم يمكنه عن النفحة فصار متعديا في الإيقاف وشغل الطريق به فيضمنه.
قال وإن أصابت بيدها أو برجلها حصاة أو نواة أو أثارت غبارا أو حجرا صغيرا ففقأ عين إنسان أو أفسد ثوبه لم يضمن وإن كان حجرا كبيرا ضمن لأنه فى الوجه الأول لايمكن التحرز عنه إذ سير الدواب لا يعرى عنه وفى الثاني ممكن لأنه ينفك عن السير عادة إنما ذالك يتعنيف الركب والمرتدف فيما ذكرنا كالراكب لأن المعنى لا يختلف.
Warning... biting with front part of teeth, hitting with front foot, push, i.e. causing to fall from the body, hitting with stick and absolute hitting with foot, kicking is one thing, trampling is another thing.
The principle is that passing on the road of Muslims is permissible, conditioned on safety, because he acts in his own right in one respect and in the right of another in another respect, due to it being common among all people. So we said permissibility conditioned by what we mentioned so that consideration is balanced from both sides.
Then it is conditioned by the condition of safety in what can be avoided, and is not conditioned in what cannot be avoided, because that would prevent action and close its door while it is open. Avoidance of trampling and similar is possible, for it is not from the necessities of ease, so we conditioned it with the condition of safety. The kick by the leg and tail cannot be avoided while riding the animal, so it is not conditioned.
If he stops it on the road, he is liable for the kick as well, because he can avoid stopping, even if he cannot avoid the kick. So he becomes a transgressor in stopping and occupying the road, so he is liable.
He (Muhammad) said: If it hits with its hand or foot a pebble or a date pit, or raises dust or a small stone, and it puts out someone's eye or ruins his garment, he is not liable. If it is a large stone, he is liable, because in the first case avoidance is not possible, as the movement of animals is rarely free of it; in the second case it is possible, because it [raising a large stone] is customarily free from movement; it only happens due to harsh urging. The rider and the pillion-rider are alike in what we mentioned, because the meaning does not differ.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary establishes a key principle in Hanafi diyat law: the liability for injuries caused by an animal on a public road depends on whether the injury could have been avoided by the person controlling the animal. The general rule is that passing on a Muslim road is permissible but conditioned on safety. This condition applies only to harms that are avoidable. Unavoidable harms, such as a sudden kick from the hind leg or tail while riding, are not subject to liability. However, if the rider stops the animal on the road unnecessarily, he becomes a transgressor and assumes liability for even unavoidable kicks, because the stopping itself was avoidable. Regarding debris: small stones or dust kicked up normally during movement are unavoidable, so no liability; but large stones are not normal and arise from harsh urging, making the rider liable. The same rule applies to the pillion-rider (murdif) as to the rider, as the legal reasoning is identical.

Key Terms
احتراز (ihtiraz): Avoidance or precaution; the ability of the rider to prevent the harmful action.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation; the obligation to pay blood money or damages.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression; acting beyond permissible limits, making one liable for consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule in this passage, when is a rider NOT liable for an injury caused by his animal's foot on the road?
A) When the animal kicks up a large stone and injures someone.
B) When the animal tramples someone while walking.
C) When the animal kicks with its hind leg while being ridden normally.
D) When the rider stops the animal on the road and it kicks someone.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat, the rider is only liable for animal-caused injuries that could have been avoided; unavoidable harms carry no compensation.

Liability for Stones Kicked Up by a Galloping Horse
Ruling on liability for injury from horse-propelled debris

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for injuries caused by stones kicked up by a galloping horse and distinguish between avoidable and unavoidable harm.

Core Idea
Small unavoidable debris: no liability. Large avoidable stones: liability.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya explains the rule of daman (compensation liability) when a galloping horse causes injury by throwing stones or dust. The key distinction is whether the harm is usual and unavoidable or unusual and avoidable. The rider is not liable for ordinary small debris, but is liable for large stones that could be avoided. The passage also covers joint liability when two riders share control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and source of harm
Recognize the rider (raakib) and the victim. The horse is galloping, causing debris to fly.
The horse itself is not liable; liability attaches to the rider due to control.
2
Classify the debris as small or large
Small debris (dust, small pebbles, small stones) are usual and unavoidable. Large stones are unusual and can be avoided.
The passage uses the Arabic terms 'صغير' and 'كبير' for small and large.
3
Apply the principle of ihtiraz (avoidability)
If the harm is unavoidable (ihtiraz mumtani'), there is no liability. If avoidable (ihtiraz mumkin), liability applies.
Small debris is unavoidable; large stones are avoidable by controlling the horse's speed.
4
Determine liability for each case
For small debris: no daman (compensation). For large stones: daman wajib (obligatory).
The ruling is based on usual practice ('ādah).
5
Handle the two-rider scenario
If two riders share the horse, both are liable because both control the horse.
Their joint control (tasarruf) makes them jointly responsible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح گھوڑا دوڑ رہا ہے اور دوڑنے کی وجہ سے کنکریاں یا گٹھلیاں اڑ رہی ہیں یا گردوغبار اڑ رہا ہے یا چھوٹی چھوٹی پتھری اڑ رہی ہے جس سے کسی کی آنکھ پھوٹ گئی تو راکب پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر بڑا پتھر ہو تو ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اول معاف ہے اور ثانی معاف نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب گھوڑا چلے گا تو عادہ یہ امور سامنے آتے ہیں۔ گویا ان سے احتر از ناممکن ہے اور خانی سے احتراز ممکن ہے کیونکہ ایسا عادہ ہوتا ہے کہ گھوڑا دوڑتا ہے اور بڑے بڑے پتھر نہیں اڑتے بلکہ سوار جب زیادہ متی گھوڑے پر کرتا ہے تو بڑے بڑے پتھر اڑتے ہیں۔ اگر زید کے پیچھے گھوڑے پر خالد بھی ہو تو اب ضمان دونوں پر آئے گا اس لئے کہ اب گھوڑا ان دونوں کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ اور دونوں کے تصرف میں ہے۔
Explanation: A horse is galloping, and due to its running, small pebbles or pits are flying, or dust is flying, or small stones are flying, and as a result someone's eye is injured: then the rider is not liable for compensation. But if it is a large stone, then compensation becomes obligatory. The first is forgiven, and the second is not forgiven, because when the horse moves, these matters usually occur; so it is impossible to avoid them. But avoidance of the large stone is possible, because it is not usual that a horse runs and large stones fly; rather, when the rider applies excessive force to the horse, then large stones fly. If Khalid is also on the horse behind Zaid, then liability falls on both, because the horse is under the control of both, and both are acting upon it.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage explains the rule of liability (daman) for injuries caused by a galloping horse. The passage distinguishes between small, unavoidable debris (small stones, dust) and large, avoidable stones. For small debris, there is no liability because it is impossible to avoid them during normal galloping. For large stones, liability exists because their projection is not usual and can be avoided by controlling the horse's speed. The passage also covers the case of two riders: both are jointly liable because they both control the horse. This ruling is based on the principle that liability only attaches to harm that could have been avoided.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or responsibility for compensation of harm caused, whether to life, limb, or property.
راکب (raakib): A rider, the person riding the animal (horse).
احتراز (ihtiraz): Avoidance or taking precaution to prevent harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the injury was caused by his horse.
B) No, because the pebble is small and unavoidable in normal galloping.
C) Yes, because he could have avoided the pebble by slowing down.
D) No, because the pedestrian was trespassing.

Key Takeaway
Liability for injuries caused by a galloping horse depends on whether the harm was avoidable: small debris is unavoidable and thus not compensable, while large stones are avoidable and thus compensable.

Liability for Animal Waste on the Road: Movement vs. Unnecessary Stop
Ruling on liability for animal excrement with distinction between moving/necessary stop and unnecessary stop.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for harm caused by animal excrement on a public road, and distinguish between necessary (no liability) and transgressive (liable) stopping.

Core Idea
Moving or necessary stop: no liability; unnecessary stop: liability arises from transgression.

This passage from Quduri's al-Mukhtasar addresses a classic liability scenario: if an animal excretes on the road and someone slips and dies, when is the owner liable? The ruling hinges on whether the animal was moving or stopped, and if stopped, whether the stop was necessary for the animal's nature. Under the Hanafi school, necessity negates liability, while transgressive conduct creates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an animal excreting on a public road. The ruling: the owner is not liable if the animal is moving or stopped out of necessity for urination/defecation; the owner is liable if the animal is stopped for any other reason.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is not a direct textual source but rational reasoning based on the necessity of movement and the transgressive nature of unnecessary stopping. The text argues that excreting while moving is unavoidable, and some animals only do so when stopped—so stopping for that purpose is still necessity.
Hanafi usul classifies this as a dalil 'aqli (rational proof) based on custom and harm.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrases: 'min darurat al-sayr' (necessity of travel) and 'muta'addi fi hadha al-iqaf' (transgressor in this stopping). The link: if the act is necessary, there is no liability because avoidance is impossible; if the act is unnecessary and causes harm, it is transgression and liability attaches.
Notice the contrast between 'necessity' and 'transgression'—the entire ruling turns on this.
4
Apply the distinction to a new scenario
Consider a rider who stops his horse to check his phone. The horse urinates, a pedestrian slips and dies. Is the rider liable? Since the stop was not for the horse's need, it is unnecessary; thus the rider is liable (like the case in the text).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical consequence is that in courts, the burden is on the victim to prove the stop was unnecessary. If proven, the owner pays diyah (blood money). This ruling balances the needs of travelers and pedestrians.
Other schools may have different thresholds, but Hanafi law is guided by the principle of harm prevention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوپائے نے راستہ میں لید کی ہو یا پیشاب کیا حالانکہ چوپایہ چل رہا تھا کہ کوئی انسان ہلاک ہو گیا ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں
قال فإن راثت أو بالت في الطريق وهي تسير فعطب به إنسان لم يضمن لأنه من ضرورت السير فلايمكنه الاحتراز عنه وكذا إذا أوقفها لذالك لأن من الدواب ما لايفعل ذالك إلا بالإيقاف وإن أوقفها لغير ذالک فعطب إنسان بروثها أو بولها ضمن لأنه متعد فى هذا الإيقاف لأنه ليس من ضرورات السير ثم هو أكثر ضررا بالمارة من السير لما أنه أدوم منه فلا يلحق به
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر چوپائے نے لید کی ہو یا راستہ میں پیشاب کیا حالانکہ چوپایہ چل رہا ہے پس اس سے کوئی انسان ہلاک ہو گیا تو وہ ضامن نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ سیر ضروریات میں سے ہے پس اس کو اس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جب کہ اس نے چوپائے کو اس کے لئے (لید یا پیشاب کے لئے ٹھہرایا ہو اس لئے کہ بعض چوپائے یہ کام نہیں کرتے مگر کھڑا کرنے کے ساتھ اور اگر اس کو اسکے غیر کے لئے کھڑا کیا ہوپس کوئی انسان اس کی لید یا پیشاب کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہو گیا تو وہ ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ اس ایقاف میں متعدی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ایقاف) چلنے کی ضروریات میں نہیں ہے پھر ایقاف را بگیروں کے لئے سیر سے زیادہ مضر ہے اس لئے کہ ایقاف سیر سے زیادہ دائی ہے تو ایقاف سمیر کے ساتھ لاحق نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح اگر گھوڑے نے راستہ میں لید کردی یا پیشاب کر دیا تو چونکہ اس سے احتراز غیر ممکن ہے لہذا اگر اس میں پھسل کر کوئی شخص مر جائے تو را کب پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح کچھ چوپائے ایسے ہوتے ہیں جو کھڑے ہو کر لید کرتے ہیں یا موتتے ہیں اس لئے راکب نے اس کو کھڑا کر دیا تا کہ اپنی ضروریات سے فارغ ہو جائے تو چونکہ اس کے کھڑا کرنے میں ضرورت تھی اس لئے اب بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر ایسے ہی راستہ میں کھڑا کر دیا ہو پھر اس نے لید یا گو بر کیا اور کوئی اس میں پھسل کر مر گیا تو اب مالک پر ضمان آئے گا کیونکہ یہ کھڑا کرنا بے ضرورت ہے اس لئے وہ اس میں متعدی ہو گیا لہذا ضمان آئے گا راستہ چلنے والوں کو گھوڑے کے چلنے سے اتنی دقت نہ ہوگی جتنی اس کے کھڑے ہونے سے ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ سیر میں دوام نہیں اور وقوف میں دوام ہے جو ٹریفک روک سکتا ہے اس لئے ایقاف کو سیر کا درجہ نہیں دیا جائے گا بلکہ سیر کو غیر مضمون اور ایقاف کو مضمون قرار دیا جائے گا۔
If the animal excretes or urinates on the road while it is moving, and a person perishes because of it, he is not liable, because it is a necessity of movement and he cannot avoid it. Similarly, if he stops it for that (excretion), because some animals do not do that except when stopped. But if he stops it for other than that, and a person perishes because of its excrement or urine, he is liable, because he is transgressing in this stopping, as it is not from the necessities of movement. Moreover, it is more harmful to passers-by than movement because it is more persistent, so it is not treated like movement. Translation: Al-Quduri said: So if the animal excreted or urinated on the road while it is moving, and a person perishes from it, he is not liable because this is from the necessities of movement, so avoidance is not possible. Similarly, when he stopped the animal for that (excretion), because some animals do that only when stopped. But if he stopped it for other than that, and a person perishes from its excrement or urine, he is liable because he is transgressing in this stopping, as this stopping is not from the necessities of movement. Furthermore, stopping is more harmful to passers-by than movement because it is more enduring, so stopping is not likened to movement. Explanation: If a horse excreted or urinated on the road, and since avoidance is impossible, if a person slips on it and dies, the rider is not liable. Similarly, some animals only excrete or urinate when standing, so if the rider stopped it to relieve itself, then because stopping was necessary, there is no liability. But if he stopped it without need, and it excreted or defecated, and someone slips and dies, then the owner is liable, because this stopping was without need, so he became a transgressor; therefore liability applies. Passers-by are not inconvenienced as much by the movement of the horse as by its stopping, because movement has no continuity, but stopping has continuity which can block traffic. So stopping is not given the status of movement; rather movement is not liable and stopping is liable.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on liability for death caused by slipping on animal excrement or urine on a public road. The primary source is a statement from Quduri's al-Mukhtasar. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If the animal is moving or stopped out of necessity (e.g., to relieve itself), there is no liability because the excrement is unavoidable in the course of travel or a necessary stop. (2) If the animal is stopped unnecessarily, then the owner becomes a transgressor (muta'addi) and is liable for any resulting harm. The reasoning is that unnecessary stopping is more harmful to passers-by than movement because it is continuous (e.g., blocking traffic). Hence, the ruling treats movement as non-liable (ghayr madmun) and unnecessary stopping as liable (madmun).

Key Terms
لید (layd): Animal dung or excrement.
ایقاف (īqāf): Stopping or halting the animal, particularly in the context of causing a hazard on the road.
متعدی (muta'addī): One who transgresses or exceeds the bounds of what is permissible, incurring liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A rider stops his horse in the middle of the road to tie his shoelace. The horse defecates, a pedestrian slips on it and dies. Is the rider liable?
A) No, because defecation is natural.
B) No, because the rider did not intend harm.
C) Yes, because the stop was unnecessary and thus transgressive.
D) Yes, because the horse should be removed immediately.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability for harm from animal waste hinges on whether the waste is unavoidable (movement/necessary stop) or the result of an unnecessary, transgressive stop.

Liability for Animal Kicks: The Driver and Leader
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for animal kicks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the driver's liability for a hind kick, apply the majority's principle of preventability, and distinguish between kicks and bites.

Core Idea
A driver is not liable for a hind kick because prevention is impossible, unlike a bite controllable by reins.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi disagreement about liability for animal-caused injuries. The initial view of Imam al-Quduri held both driver and leader liable based on sight, but the majority of later Hanafi scholars refined this ruling by focusing on the ability to prevent harm. Understanding this refinement teaches a key principle: liability in Hanafi law depends on effective control, not merely on observation.

Guided Path
1
State the initial ruling (Quduri's view)
Identify what the driver and leader are liable for according to al-Quduri. Note the basis: visibility. Driver sees both front and hind legs, so liable for both. Leader sees only front, so liable only for front leg injuries.
The term for kick is 'najha', distinguished from bite 'kadm'.
2
Identify the refinement (majority view)
Understand why the majority rejects driver liability for hind kicks. Their reasoning: even if the driver sees the kick, there is no means to prevent it (e.g., no reins on the hind leg). Thus, liability cannot attach.
This is a 'talil' argument based on capability of prevention.
3
Contrast with the bite case
Explain why a bite is treated differently: a bite can be prevented by pulling the reins. This illustrates the principle of 'imkan al-ihraz' (possibility of prevention).
The bite case is used as a proof by distinction (tafriq).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare outcomes: under Quduri, driver liable for all leg injuries; under majority, driver not liable for hind kicks but still liable for bites and front leg injuries.
The practical difference is significant for legal claims.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the majority view is deemed 'al-ashah' (most correct). The text notes that most copies of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar actually support the majority view, according to Allamah Ayni.
The mufta bihi position is the majority view.

Source Text

سائق اور قائد کب ضامن ہوتے ہیں
والسائق ضامن لما أصابت بيدها أو رجلها والقائد ضامن لما أصابت بيدها دون رجلها والمراد النفحة قال رضى الله عنه هكذا ذكره القدورى فى مختصره وإليه مال بعض المشايخ ووجهه أن النفحة بمراى عين السائق فيمكنه الاحتراز عنه وغائب عن بصر القائد فلا يمكنه التحرز عنه
ترجمہ اور پیچھے سے ہانکنے والا ضامن ہے اس چیز کا جس کو چو پایہ پہنچا ہوا اگلے پاؤں یا پچھلے پاؤں سے اور قائد ( آگے سے کھینچنے والا ) ضامن ہے اس چیز کا جو پہنچا ہو اپنے اگلے پاؤں سے نہ کہ اپنے پچھلے پاؤں سے اور مراد پاؤں سے پہنچنے سے ) نفحہ ہے۔ (کھر سے مارنا ) مصنف نے فرمایا اس کو قدوری نے اپنی مختصر میں ایسے ہی ذکر کیا ہے اور اس کی جانب بعض مشائخ کا میلان ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فتحہ سائق کی آنکھ کے سامنے ہے تو اس کو اس سے احتراز ممکن ہے اور قائد کی آنکھ سے غائب ہے تو اس کو اس سے احتراز ناممکن ہے۔
تشریح اگر سائق چوپائے کو ہانکے جا رہا ہے تو اگلے پاؤں سے روند نا اور پچھلے پاؤں سے روند نا برابر ہے، بہر دوصورت سائق پر ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اور اگر قائد ہے تو وہ پچھلے پاؤں کا ذمہ دار نہیں ہے بلکہ صرف اگلے پاؤں کا ذمہ دار ہے اس لئے کہ سائق کے سامنے دونوں پاؤں ہیں تو اس سے احتراز کر سکتا ہے اور چونکہ قائد کی نظر پچھلے پاؤں پر نہیں تو اس کے لئے اس سے احتراز بھی ممکن نہیں اس لئے وہ پچھلے پاؤں کا ضامن نہ ہوگا ، شیخ قدوری نے مختصر القدوری میں یہی بیان کیا ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ عراق کا یہی مختار ہے۔
سائق نفحہ کا ضامن نہیں
وقال أكثر المشايخ إن السائق لا يضمن النفحة أيضا وإن كان يراها إذ ليس على رجلها ما يمنعها به فلايمكنه التحرز عنه بخلاف الكدم لإمكانه كبحها يلجامها وبهذا ينطق أكثر النسخ وهو الأصح
ترجمہ اور اکثر مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ سائق بھی نفحہ کا ضامن نہ ہوگا اگر چہ وہ اس کو دیکھتا ہے اس لئے کہ چوپائے کے پاؤں پر ایسی چیز نہیں ہے جو اس کو لات مارنے سے روک دے تو اس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے، بخلاف کاٹنے کے اس کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا لگام کھینچنے کی وجہ سے اور اسی کے ساتھ قدوری کے اکثر نسخے ناطق ہیں ، اور یہی اصح ہے۔
تشریح امام قدوری نے جو فرمایا ہے وہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے، یہاں سے مشائخ ماوراء النہر کا قول بیان کرتے ہیں ۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ پچھلی لات کا ضمان جس طرح قائد پر نہیں ہے اسی طرح سائق پر بھی نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اگر چہ سائق اس کو دیکھ تو رہا ہے لیکن چوپائے کے پاؤں پر کوئی ایسی چیز بندھی ہوئی نہیں ہے جس کی وجہ سے اس کو لات مارنے سے روکا جا سکے لہذا اس سے احتر از غیر ممکن ہے ہاں اگر چوپایہ دانت سے کالے تو اس سے احتراز ممکن ہے یعنی اس کی لگام کھینچ کر اس کو روکا جاسکتا ہے۔ بقول علامہ عینی قدوری کے اکثر نسخے اسی کے ناطق ہیں اور اصبح بھی یہی قول ہے کہ سائق اور قائد دونوں کا ایک ہی حکم ہے، فیہ مافیہ، کج ، چوپائے کا لگام کھینچنا۔
When is the driver and leader liable? The driver is liable for what the animal hits with its hand or foot, and the leader is liable for what it hits with its hand, not its foot. And what is meant by foot is the kick. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Thus al-Quduri mentioned it in his Mukhtasar, and some mashayikh inclined to this. Its reason is that the kick is before the eyes of the driver, so he can avoid it, and it is absent from the sight of the leader, so he cannot avoid it. Translation: The one who drives from behind is liable for what the animal strikes with its front leg or hind leg, and the leader (who pulls from the front) is liable for what it strikes with its front leg, not its hind leg. And what is meant by striking with the leg is the kick. The author said: Al-Quduri mentioned it thus in his Mukhtasar, and some mashayikh inclined to it. The reason is that the kick is before the eyes of the driver, so he can avoid it, and it is absent from the sight of the leader, so he cannot avoid it. Explanation: If the driver is driving the animal, trampling with the front leg and hind leg are equal; in both cases the driver is liable. But if it is a leader, he is not responsible for the hind leg, only for the front leg, because both legs are in front of the driver, so he can avoid; and because the leader's vision is not on the hind leg, he cannot avoid it, so he is not liable for the hind leg. Shaykh al-Quduri stated this in his al-Mukhtasar, and some mashayikh of Iraq adopt this. The driver is not liable for the kick. And the majority of mashayikh said: The driver is also not liable for the kick, even though he sees it, because the animal has nothing on its foot to prevent it, so he cannot avoid it, unlike the bite, because it is possible to restrain it by its reins. Most copies of al-Quduri state this, and it is the most correct. Translation: And the majority of mashayikh said that the driver also will not be liable for the kick, even if he sees it, because there is nothing on the animal's foot to prevent it, so avoidance is not possible. In contrast to the bite, because its avoidance is possible by pulling its reins. Most copies of al-Quduri are explicit on this, and this is the most correct. Explanation: The statement of Imam al-Quduri has already passed. From here, the saying of the mashayikh of Transoxiana is related. The sum of it is that liability for the hind kick is not on the leader, and similarly not on the driver. Because even though the driver sees it, there is nothing tied to the animal's foot by which it can be prevented from kicking, so avoidance is impossible. Yes, if the animal bites with its teeth, avoidance is possible by pulling its reins. According to Allamah Ayni, most copies of al-Quduri state this, and the most correct view is that driver and leader have the same ruling. [Fih ma fih, kuj, pulling the animal's reins.]
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a driver (sa'iq) who drives an animal from behind and a leader (qa'id) who leads it from the front for injuries caused by the animal's front and hind legs. The initial ruling from Quduri and some Iraqi mashayikh states that the driver is liable for both front and hind leg injuries because both are in his sight, whereas the leader is only liable for front leg injuries because the hind leg is out of his sight. However, the majority of mashayikh (from Transoxiana) refine this ruling: they hold that the driver is also not liable for the hind leg's kick (najha) because, although he sees it, he cannot prevent a kick as there is no means to control the hind leg, unlike a bite which can be prevented by pulling the reins. The text concludes that this latter view is the most correct (al-ashah), and most copies of Quduri's work actually support this. The practical consequence: both driver and leader are not liable for hind leg kicks, but both are liable for bites because they can be prevented by reins.

Key Terms
سائق (sā'iq): The person who drives an animal from behind, making it move forward.
قائد (qā'id): The person who leads an animal from the front, pulling it.
نفحة (najḥa): A kick or strike with the hind foot, specifically the act of kicking.
کدم (kadm): A bite or injury caused by the animal's teeth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A driver (sa'iq) drives a horse from behind. The horse kicks a pedestrian with its hind leg, causing injury. According to the majority (al-ashah) Hanafi position, is the driver liable?
A) Yes, because he is driving the horse.
B) Yes, because he could see the kick approaching.
C) No, because a hind kick cannot be prevented even if seen.
D) No, only the leader is liable for hind kicks.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability for animal injuries hinges on the ability to prevent harm, not merely on seeing it.

Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Liability for a Horse's Kick
Presents the Shafi'i position on joint liability for a horse's kick and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability for a horse's kick and explain why the Shafi'i argument is rejected based on the principle of incomplete coercion.

Core Idea
The hadith 'al-rajulu jubbār' exempts the horse's kick from liability, and incomplete coercion does not transfer the act.

This passage examines a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding liability when a horse causes death by its kick. Imam Shafi'i holds the rider, driver, and leader jointly liable because the horse's act is attributed to them. The Hanafi school rebuts this using the Prophetic hadith 'al-rajulu jubbār' and the usul principle that acts only transfer under complete coercion (ikrāh kāmil). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply hadith and legal principles in diyat cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
What does Imam Shafi'i claim? The rider, driver, and leader are all liable for the horse's kick because the act is attributed to them.
2
Identify the Hanafi primary proof
The hadith 'al-rajulu jubbār' (the leg is free) is the primary proof. How does this exempt the kick?
3
Analyze the transfer of act argument
The Shafi'i claim of attribution is met with the Hanafi response: transfer only occurs with complete coercion (threat of killing), not incomplete coercion (threat of beating). Why is this distinction crucial?
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi says no diyah or kaffarah; Shafi'i says all three must pay blood money.

امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
قال الشافعي يضمنون النفحة كلهم لأن فعلها مضاف إليهم والحجة عليه ما ذكرناه وقوله عليه السلام الرجل جبار معناه النفحة بالرجل وانتقال الفعل بتخويف القتل كما في المكره وهذا تخويف بالضرب ترجمہ شافعی نے فرمایا کہ نتیجہ کے یہ تمام ضامن ہوں گے اس لئے کہ اس کا فعل انہیں کی جانب مضاف ہوگا اور ان کے خلاف حجت وہ ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان کہ پاؤں بدر ہے اس کے معنی لات مارنا ہے اور فعل کا انتقال قتل کا خوف دلانے سے ہوتا ہے جیسے مگرہ میں اور یہ ضرب کی تخویف ہے۔ تشریح امام شافعی کے نزدیک لات مارنے کا بھی ضمان ہو گا خواہ را کب ہو یا سائق و قائد کیونکہ گھوڑے کا فعل ان کی جانب منسوب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ ہماری مذکورہ دلیل ان پر حجت ہے اور ان پر یہ حدیث حجت ہے جو حضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ الرجــل جبار یعنی پاؤں سے جو مر جائے تو اس کا عمان واجب نہ ہوگا ۔
پھر امام شافعی نے جو فرمایا ہے کہ چوپائے کا فعل ان کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا یہ بھی خلاف اصول ہے، کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ فعل کا انتقال تخویف کامل اور کراو کامل کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے اور یہاں اکراہ کامل نہیں بلکہ اکراہ ناقص ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے گھوڑے کو قتل کی دھمکی نہیں بلکہ ضرب کی دی ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام یا کراہ ناقص ہے۔
Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint: He said that they all guarantee the kick because its act is attributed to them. The proof against him is what we mentioned, and his statement, peace be upon him: 'The foot is free' meaning the kick by the foot, and transfer of the act occurs by threat of killing as in coercion, and this is a threat by beating. Translation: Shafi'i said that all of them will be liable for the result because the act is attributed to them, and the proof against them is what we have already mentioned, and the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, that 'the foot is free' means a kick by the foot is not liable. Commentary: According to Shafi'i, liability for a kick applies whether it is the rider, driver, or leader, because the horse's act is attributed to them. The author of Hidayah said that our mentioned proof is an argument against them, and this hadith is an argument against them that the Prophet said: 'The foot is free' meaning if someone dies from a foot, its blood money is not obligatory. Then Shafi'i's claim that the animal's act transfers to them is also against principles. Why? Because transfer of act only occurs in case of complete threat and complete coercion, and here the coercion is not complete but incomplete because they threatened the horse with beating, not killing. In summary, the coercion is incomplete.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding liability when a horse causes death by kicking. Imam Shafi'i holds that the rider, driver, and leader are all jointly liable (daman) for the kick because the horse's act is attributed to them. The Hanafi response, as stated by the author of al-Hidayah, relies on the hadith 'al-rajulu jubbār' (the leg is free), meaning that if someone dies from a kick by a leg (of an animal), there is no liability. The Hanafis argue that the act cannot be transferred to the humans except in cases of complete coercion (ikrāh kāmil), such as threatening to kill the animal. Here, the humans only threatened the horse with beating, which is incomplete coercion (ikrāh nāqis), so the act remains the horse's own and no liability attaches to the humans. The text follows the order: first stating the Shafi'i position, then the Hanafi proof from hadith, then a detailed refutation of the Shafi'i argument about transfer of act.

Key Terms
الرجل جبار (al-rajulu jubbār): A hadith meaning the foot (of an animal) is free from liability for any death it causes.
نفحة (najah): A kick from the hind leg of a horse or similar animal.
اکراہ ناقص (ikrāh nāqis): Incomplete coercion where the threat is not severe enough to transfer the act to the coercer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument, why is the rider not liable for the horse's kick?
A) Because the rider is not the direct cause
B) Because the Prophet said 'al-rajulu jubbār' (the leg is free)
C) Because the horse was coerced
D) Because the kick is always accidental

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts liability for a horse's kick based on the hadith 'al-rajulu jubbār' and the principle that incomplete coercion does not transfer the act.
